					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Fictional character created by J. R. R. Tolkien</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1033289096">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Gandalf_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Gandalf (disambiguation)">Gandalf (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p class="mw-empty-elt">


</p>
<div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Fictional character</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1066479718">.mw-parser-output .infobox-subbox{padding:0;border:none;margin:-3px;width:auto;min-width:100%;font-size:100%;clear:none;float:none;background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .infobox-3cols-child{margin:auto}.mw-parser-output .infobox .navbar{font-size:100%}body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-header,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-subheader,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-above,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-title,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-image,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-full-data,body.skin-minerva .mw-parser-output .infobox-below{text-align:center}</style><table class="infobox" style="border-spacing: 2px 5px;"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-above" style="background-color: #DEDEE2;">Gandalf</th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-subheader"><i><a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">Tolkien</a></i> character</td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="infobox-image"><span class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Frameless"><a href="/wiki/File:Gandalf_from_The_Trolls_are_Turned_to_Stone_-_J.R.R_Tolkien.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/bd/Gandalf_from_The_Trolls_are_Turned_to_Stone_-_J.R.R_Tolkien.jpg/220px-Gandalf_from_The_Trolls_are_Turned_to_Stone_-_J.R.R_Tolkien.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/bd/Gandalf_from_The_Trolls_are_Turned_to_Stone_-_J.R.R_Tolkien.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="311" data-file-height="245" /></a></span><div class="infobox-caption">Detail of Gandalf (right) turning the trolls to stone in one of J.R.R. Tolkien's drawings for <i>The Hobbit</i></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">First appearance</th><td class="infobox-data"><i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i> (1937)</td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Last appearance</th><td class="infobox-data"><i><a href="/wiki/Unfinished_Tales" title="Unfinished Tales">Unfinished Tales</a></i> (1980)</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" class="infobox-header" style="background-color: #DEDEE2;">In-universe information</th></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Aliases</th><td class="infobox-data">See <a href="#Names">Names</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Race</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Maia_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Maia (Middle-earth)">Maia</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Affiliation</th><td class="infobox-data"><a href="/wiki/Fellowship_of_the_Ring_(characters)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellowship of the Ring (characters)">Company of the Ring</a></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" class="infobox-label">Weapon</th><td class="infobox-data"><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1126788409">.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul{line-height:inherit;list-style:none;margin:0;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .plainlist ol li,.mw-parser-output .plainlist ul li{margin-bottom:0}</style><div class="plainlist">
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Glamdring" class="mw-redirect" title="Glamdring">Glamdring</a></li>
<li>Wizard's staff</li></ul>
</div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><b>Gandalf</b> is a protagonist in <a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a>'s novels <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>. He is a <a href="/wiki/Wizards_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wizards (Middle-earth)">wizard</a>, one of the Istari order, and the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Fellowship_of_the_Ring_(characters)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellowship of the Ring (characters)">Fellowship of the Ring</a>. Tolkien took the name "Gandalf" from the <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> <a href="/wiki/Dvergatal" class="mw-redirect" title="Dvergatal">"Catalogue of Dwarves" (<i>Dvergatal</i>)</a> in the <i>Völuspá</i>.
</p><p>As a wizard and the bearer of one of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Rings" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Rings">Three Rings</a>, Gandalf has great power, but works mostly by encouraging and persuading. He sets out as Gandalf the Grey, possessing great knowledge and travelling continually. Gandalf is focused on the mission to counter the Dark Lord <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">Sauron</a> by destroying the <a href="/wiki/One_Ring" title="One Ring">One Ring</a>. He is associated with fire; his ring of power is <a href="/wiki/Narya" class="mw-redirect" title="Narya">Narya</a>, the Ring of Fire. As such, he delights in <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">fireworks</a> to entertain the <a href="/wiki/Hobbit" title="Hobbit">hobbits</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Shire" title="The Shire">the Shire</a>, while in great need he uses fire as a weapon. As one of the <a href="/wiki/Maiar" title="Maiar">Maiar</a>, he is an immortal spirit from <a href="/wiki/Valinor" title="Valinor">Valinor</a>, but his physical body can be killed. 
</p><p>In <i>The Hobbit</i>, Gandalf assists the 13 dwarves and the hobbit <a href="/wiki/Bilbo_Baggins" title="Bilbo Baggins">Bilbo Baggins</a> with <a href="/wiki/Quests_in_Middle-earth" title="Quests in Middle-earth">their quest</a> to retake the <a href="/wiki/Lonely_Mountain" title="Lonely Mountain">Lonely Mountain</a> from <a href="/wiki/Smaug" title="Smaug">Smaug</a> the dragon, but leaves them to urge the <b>White Council</b> to expel Sauron from his fortress of <a href="/wiki/Dol_Guldur" class="mw-redirect" title="Dol Guldur">Dol Guldur</a>. In the course of the quest, Bilbo finds a magical ring. The expulsion succeeds, but in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, Gandalf reveals that Sauron's retreat was only a feint, as he soon reappeared in <a href="/wiki/Mordor" title="Mordor">Mordor</a>. Gandalf further explains that, after years of investigation, he is sure that Bilbo's ring is the One Ring that Sauron needs to dominate the whole of Middle-earth. The <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Elrond" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Elrond">Council of Elrond</a> creates the Fellowship of the Ring, with Gandalf as its leader, to defeat Sauron by destroying the Ring. He takes them south through the Misty Mountains, but is killed fighting a <a href="/wiki/Balrog" title="Balrog">Balrog</a>, an evil spirit-being, in the underground realm of <a href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moria (Middle-earth)">Moria</a>. After he dies, he is sent back to Middle-earth to complete his mission as Gandalf the White. He reappears to three of the Fellowship and helps to counter the enemy in <a href="/wiki/Rohan_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rohan (Middle-earth)">Rohan</a>, then in <a href="/wiki/Gondor" title="Gondor">Gondor</a>, and finally at the <a href="/wiki/Black_Gate_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Gate (Middle-earth)">Black Gate</a> of Mordor, in each case largely by offering guidance. When victory is complete, he crowns Aragorn as King before leaving Middle-earth for ever to return to Valinor.
</p><p>Tolkien once described Gandalf as an <a href="/wiki/Angel" title="Angel">angel</a> incarnate; later, both he and other scholars have likened Gandalf to the <a href="/wiki/Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology">Norse god</a> <a href="/wiki/Odin" title="Odin">Odin</a> in his "Wanderer" guise. Others have described Gandalf as a guide-figure who assists the protagonists, comparable to the <a href="/wiki/Cumaean_Sibyl" title="Cumaean Sibyl">Cumaean Sibyl</a> who assisted <a href="/wiki/Aeneas" title="Aeneas">Aeneas</a> in <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Aeneid" class="mw-redirect" title="The Aeneid">The Aeneid</a></i>, or to Virgil himself in <a href="/wiki/Dante" class="mw-redirect" title="Dante">Dante</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Inferno_(Dante)" title="Inferno (Dante)">Inferno</a></i>. Scholars have likened his return in white to the <a href="/wiki/Transfiguration_of_Jesus" title="Transfiguration of Jesus">transfiguration of Christ</a>; he is further described as a <a href="/wiki/Prophet" title="Prophet">prophet</a>, representing one element of Christ's <a href="/wiki/Threefold_office" title="Threefold office">threefold office</a> of prophet, priest, and king, where the other two roles are taken by <a href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins" title="Frodo Baggins">Frodo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a>. 
</p><p>The Gandalf character has been featured in radio, television, stage, video game, music, and film adaptations, including <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bakshi" title="Ralph Bakshi">Ralph Bakshi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1978_film)" title="The Lord of the Rings (1978 film)">1978 animated film</a>. His best-known portrayal is by <a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a> in <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a>'s 2001–2003 <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> film series, where the actor based his acclaimed performance on Tolkien himself. McKellen reprised the role in Jackson's 2012–2014 film series <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)" title="The Hobbit (film series)">The Hobbit</a></i>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Names">Names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Names"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Emblema_Gandalf.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emblema_Gandalf.svg/110px-Emblema_Gandalf.svg.png" decoding="async" width="110" height="121" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emblema_Gandalf.svg/165px-Emblema_Gandalf.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Emblema_Gandalf.svg/220px-Emblema_Gandalf.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="200" data-file-height="220" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Cirth" title="Cirth">Certh</a> <a href="/wiki/Rune" class="mw-redirect" title="Rune">rune</a> no. 19 "G", used by Gandalf as a personal <a href="/wiki/Sign" title="Sign">sign</a> or <a href="/wiki/Seal_(emblem)" title="Seal (emblem)">seal</a></figcaption></figure>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Tolkien derived the name <i>Gandalf</i> from Gandálfr, a <a href="/wiki/Norse_dwarf" class="mw-redirect" title="Norse dwarf">dwarf</a> in the <a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lusp%C3%A1" title="Völuspá">Völuspá</a>'s <i>Dvergatal</i>, a list of dwarf-names.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a>, the name means <i>staff-elf</i>. This is reflected in his name <i>Tharkûn</i>, which is "said to mean 'Staff-man'" in <a href="/wiki/Khuzdul" title="Khuzdul">Khuzdul</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Languages_constructed_by_J._R._R._Tolkien" title="Languages constructed by J. R. R. Tolkien">language Tolkien invented</a> for his <a href="/wiki/Dwarves_in_Middle-earth" title="Dwarves in Middle-earth">Dwarves</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In-universe_names">In-universe names</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: In-universe names"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gandalf is given several names and epithets in Tolkien's writings. <a href="/wiki/Faramir" title="Faramir">Faramir</a> calls him the Grey Pilgrim, and reports Gandalf as saying, "Many are my names in many countries. <i>Mithrandir</i><sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;a&#93;</a></sup> among the <a href="/wiki/Elf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elf (Middle-earth)">Elves</a>, Tharkûn to the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dwarf (Middle-earth)">Dwarves</a>, <a href="#Valinor">Olórin I was in my youth in the West</a> that is forgotten, in the South Incánus, in the North <i>Gandalf</i>; to <a href="/wiki/Rh%C3%BBn" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhûn">the East</a> I go not."<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;T 2&#93;</a></sup> In an early draft of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i>, he is called <i>Bladorthin</i>, while the name Gandalf is used by the dwarf who later became <a href="/wiki/Thorin_Oakenshield" title="Thorin Oakenshield">Thorin Oakenshield</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Each <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wizard (Middle-earth)">Wizard</a> is distinguished by the colour of his cloak. For most of his manifestation as a wizard, Gandalf's cloak is grey, hence the names Gandalf <i>the Grey</i> and Greyhame, from Old English <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/hame" class="extiw" title="wikt:hame">hame</a>, "cover, skin". <i>Mithrandir</i> is a name in <a href="/wiki/Sindarin" title="Sindarin">Sindarin</a> meaning "the Grey Pilgrim" or "the Grey Wanderer". Midway through <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, Gandalf becomes the head of the order of Wizards, and is renamed <a href="#Gandalf_the_White">Gandalf the White</a>. This change in status (and clothing) introduces another name for the wizard: the White Rider. However, characters who speak Elvish still refer to him as <i>Mithrandir</i>. At times in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, other characters address Gandalf by insulting nicknames: Stormcrow, <i>Láthspell</i> ("Ill-news" in <a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a>), and "Grey Fool".<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Characteristics">Characteristics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Characteristics"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Tolkien describes Gandalf as the last of the wizards to appear in <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a>, one who "seemed the least, less tall than the others, and in looks more aged, grey-haired and grey-clad, and leaning on a <a href="/wiki/Magic_(Middle-earth)#Magic_items" class="mw-redirect" title="Magic (Middle-earth)">staff</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup> Yet the <a href="/wiki/Elf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elf (Middle-earth)">Elf</a> <a href="/wiki/C%C3%ADrdan" class="mw-redirect" title="Círdan">Círdan</a> who met him on arrival nevertheless considered him "the greatest spirit and the wisest" and gave him the Elven <a href="/wiki/Three_Rings" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Rings">Ring of Power</a> called <a href="/wiki/Narya" class="mw-redirect" title="Narya">Narya</a>, the Ring of Fire, containing a "red" stone for his aid and comfort. Tolkien explicitly links Gandalf to the element <a href="/wiki/Fire_(classical_element)" title="Fire (classical element)">fire</a> later in the same essay:<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1211633275">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 32px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Warm and eager was his spirit (and it was enhanced by the ring Narya), for he was the Enemy of <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">Sauron</a>, opposing the fire that devours and wastes with the fire that kindles, and succours in wanhope and distress; but his joy, and his swift wrath, were veiled in garments grey as ash, so that only those that knew him well glimpsed the flame that was within. Merry he could be, and kindly to the young and simple, yet quick at times to sharp speech and the rebuking of folly; but he was not proud, and sought neither power nor praise ... Mostly he journeyed tirelessly on foot, leaning on a staff, and so he was called among <a href="/wiki/Man_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Man (Middle-earth)">Men</a> of the North Gandalf 'the <a href="/wiki/Elf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elf (Middle-earth)">Elf</a> of the Wand'. For they deemed him (though in error) to be of Elven-kind, since he would at times work wonders among them, loving especially the beauty of fire; and yet such marvels he wrought mostly for mirth and delight, and desired not that any should hold him in awe or take his counsels out of fear. ... Yet it is said that in the ending of the task for which he came he suffered greatly, and was slain, and being sent back from death for a brief while was clothed then in white, and became a radiant flame (yet veiled still save in great need).<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fictional_biography">Fictional biography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Fictional biography"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Valinor">Valinor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Valinor"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Valinor" title="Valinor">Valinor</a>, Gandalf was called <i>Olórin</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup> He was one of the Maiar of Valinor, specifically, one of the people of the Vala <a href="/wiki/Manw%C3%AB_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Manwë (Middle-earth)">Manwë</a>; he was said to be the wisest of the Maiar. He was closely associated with two other Valar: Irmo, in whose gardens he lived, and <a href="/wiki/Nienna" class="mw-redirect" title="Nienna">Nienna</a>, the patron of mercy, who gave him tutelage. When the Valar decided to send the order of the <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wizard (Middle-earth)">Wizards (Istari)</a> across the <a href="/wiki/Belegaer" class="mw-redirect" title="Belegaer">Great Sea</a> to <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a> to counsel and assist all those who opposed <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">Sauron</a>, Olórin was proposed by Manwë. Olórin initially begged to be excused, declaring he was too weak and that he feared Sauron, but Manwë replied that that was all the more reason for him to go.<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As one of the Maiar, Gandalf was not a mortal Man but an angelic being who had taken human form. As one of those spirits, Olórin was in service to the Creator (<a href="/wiki/Eru_Il%C3%BAvatar" class="mw-redirect" title="Eru Ilúvatar">Eru Ilúvatar</a>) and the Creator's '<a href="/wiki/Secret_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Secret Fire">Secret Fire</a>'. Along with the other Maiar who entered into Middle-earth as the five Wizards, he took on the specific form of an old man as a sign of his <a href="/wiki/Humility" title="Humility">humility</a>. The role of the wizards was to advise and counsel but never to attempt to match Sauron's strength with their own. It might be, too, that the kings and lords of Middle-earth would be more receptive to the advice of a humble old man than a more glorious form giving them direct commands.<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Middle-earth"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The wizards arrived in <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a> separately, early in the <a href="/wiki/Third_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Age">Third Age</a>; Gandalf was the last, landing in the Havens of Mithlond. He seemed the oldest and least in stature, but <a href="/wiki/C%C3%ADrdan" class="mw-redirect" title="Círdan">Círdan</a> the Shipwright felt that he was the greatest on their first meeting in the Havens, and gave him <a href="/wiki/Narya" class="mw-redirect" title="Narya">Narya</a>, the Ring of Fire. <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">Saruman</a>, the chief Wizard, learned of the gift and resented it. Gandalf hid the ring well, and it was not widely known until he left with the other <a href="/wiki/Ring-bearers" class="mw-redirect" title="Ring-bearers">ring-bearers</a> at the end of the Third Age that he, and not Círdan, was the holder of the third of the <a href="/wiki/Three_Rings" class="mw-redirect" title="Three Rings">Elven-rings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gandalf's relationship with Saruman, the head of their Order, was strained. The Wizards were commanded to aid <a href="/wiki/Man_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Man (Middle-earth)">Men</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Elf (Middle-earth)">Elves</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dwarf (Middle-earth)">Dwarves</a>, but only through counsel; they were forbidden to use force to dominate them, though Saruman increasingly disregarded this.<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_White_Council">The White Council</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The White Council"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">"White Council" redirects here. For the unreleased video game, see <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_White_Council" title="The Lord of the Rings: The White Council">The Lord of the Rings: The White Council</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/White_Council_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="White Council (disambiguation)">White Council (disambiguation)</a>.</div>
<p>Gandalf suspected early on that an evil presence, the <a href="/wiki/Sauron#The_Necromancer_of_Dol_Guldur" title="Sauron">Necromancer of Dol Guldur</a>, was not a <a href="/wiki/Nazg%C3%BBl" title="Nazgûl">Nazgûl</a> but Sauron himself. He went to <a href="/wiki/Dol_Guldur" class="mw-redirect" title="Dol Guldur">Dol Guldur</a><sup id="cite_ref-AppB_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AppB-6">&#91;T 3&#93;</a></sup> to discover the truth, but the Necromancer withdrew before him, only to return with greater force,<sup id="cite_ref-AppB_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AppB-6">&#91;T 3&#93;</a></sup> and the White Council was formed in response.<sup id="cite_ref-AppB_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AppB-6">&#91;T 3&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Galadriel" title="Galadriel">Galadriel</a> had hoped Gandalf would lead the council, but he refused, declining to be bound by any but the Valar who had sent him. Saruman was chosen instead, as the most knowledgeable about Sauron's work in the <a href="/wiki/Second_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Second Age">Second Age</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Of_the_Rings_of_Power_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Of_the_Rings_of_Power-7">&#91;T 4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gandalf returned to Dol Guldur "at great peril" and learned that the Necromancer was indeed Sauron. The following year a White Council was held, and Gandalf urged that Sauron be driven out.<sup id="cite_ref-AppB_6-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AppB-6">&#91;T 3&#93;</a></sup> Saruman, however, reassured the Council that Sauron's evident effort to find the <a href="/wiki/One_Ring" title="One Ring">One Ring</a> would fail, as the Ring would long since have been carried by the river <a href="/wiki/Anduin" class="mw-redirect" title="Anduin">Anduin</a> to the Sea; and the matter was allowed to rest. But Saruman began actively seeking the Ring near the <a href="/wiki/Gladden_Fields" class="mw-redirect" title="Gladden Fields">Gladden Fields</a> where <a href="/wiki/Isildur" title="Isildur">Isildur</a> had been killed.<sup id="cite_ref-Of_the_Rings_of_Power_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Of_the_Rings_of_Power-7">&#91;T 4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Quest_of_Erebor">The Quest of Erebor</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The Quest of Erebor"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/The_Quest_of_Erebor" class="mw-redirect" title="The Quest of Erebor">The Quest of Erebor</a>" in <i><a href="/wiki/Unfinished_Tales" title="Unfinished Tales">Unfinished Tales</a></i> elaborates upon the story behind <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i>. It tells of a chance meeting between Gandalf and <a href="/wiki/Thorin_Oakenshield" title="Thorin Oakenshield">Thorin Oakenshield</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dwarf (Middle-earth)">Dwarf</a>-king in exile, in the <i>Prancing Pony</i> inn at <a href="/wiki/Bree_(Middle-earth)" title="Bree (Middle-earth)">Bree</a>. Gandalf had for some time foreseen the coming war with <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">Sauron</a>, and knew that the North was especially vulnerable. If <a href="/wiki/Rivendell" title="Rivendell">Rivendell</a> were to be attacked, the <a href="/wiki/Dragon_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dragon (Middle-earth)">dragon</a> <a href="/wiki/Smaug" title="Smaug">Smaug</a> could cause great devastation. He persuaded Thorin that he could help him regain his lost territory of <a href="/wiki/Erebor" class="mw-redirect" title="Erebor">Erebor</a> from Smaug, and so the quest was born.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;T 5&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Hobbit"><i>The Hobbit</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: The Hobbit"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gandalf meets with <a href="/wiki/Bilbo_Baggins" title="Bilbo Baggins">Bilbo</a> in the opening of <i>The Hobbit</i>. He arranges for a tea party, to which he invites the thirteen dwarves, and thus arranges the travelling group central to the narrative. Gandalf contributes the map and key to Erebor to assist the quest.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;T 6&#93;</a></sup> On this quest Gandalf acquires the sword, <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Middle-earth_weapons_and_armour#Glamdring" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Middle-earth weapons and armour">Glamdring</a></i>, from the <a href="/wiki/Troll_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Troll (Middle-earth)">trolls'</a> treasure hoard.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;T 7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Elrond" title="Elrond">Elrond</a> informs them that the sword was made in <a href="/wiki/Gondolin" title="Gondolin">Gondolin</a>, a city long ago destroyed, where Elrond's father lived as a child.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;T 8&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After escaping from the <a href="/wiki/Misty_Mountains" class="mw-redirect" title="Misty Mountains">Misty Mountains</a> pursued by goblins and <a href="/wiki/Warg_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Warg (Middle-earth)">wargs</a>, the party is carried to safety by the <a href="/wiki/Eagle_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Eagle (Middle-earth)">Great Eagles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;T 9&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf then persuades <a href="/wiki/Beorn" title="Beorn">Beorn</a> to house and provision the company for the trip through <a href="/wiki/Mirkwood" title="Mirkwood">Mirkwood</a>. Gandalf leaves the company before they enter Mirkwood, saying that he had pressing business to attend to.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;T 10&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>He turns up again before the walls of Erebor disguised as an old man, revealing himself when it seems the Men of <a href="/wiki/Esgaroth" title="Esgaroth">Esgaroth</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Mirkwood_Elves" class="mw-redirect" title="Mirkwood Elves">Mirkwood Elves</a> will fight Thorin and the dwarves over Smaug's treasure. The Battle of Five Armies ensues when hosts of goblins and wargs attack all three parties.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;T 11&#93;</a></sup> After the battle, Gandalf accompanies Bilbo back to <a href="/wiki/The_Shire" title="The Shire">the Shire</a>, revealing at Rivendell what his pressing business had been: Gandalf had once again urged the council to evict Sauron, since quite evidently Sauron did not require the <a href="/wiki/One_Ring" title="One Ring">One Ring</a> to continue to attract evil to Mirkwood.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;T 12&#93;</a></sup> Then the Council "put[s] forth its power" and drives Sauron from <a href="/wiki/Dol_Guldur" class="mw-redirect" title="Dol Guldur">Dol Guldur</a>. Sauron had anticipated this, and had feigned a withdrawal, only to reappear in <a href="/wiki/Mordor" title="Mordor">Mordor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Council_of_Elrond_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Council_of_Elrond-16">&#91;T 13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Lord_of_the_Rings"><i>The Lord of the Rings</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: The Lord of the Rings"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gandalf_the_Grey">Gandalf the Grey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Gandalf the Grey"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gwaihir_the_Eagle_rescues_Gandalf_from_Orthanc_by_Alexander_Korotich.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Gwaihir_the_Eagle_rescues_Gandalf_from_Orthanc_by_Alexander_Korotich.jpg/170px-Gwaihir_the_Eagle_rescues_Gandalf_from_Orthanc_by_Alexander_Korotich.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="250" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Gwaihir_the_Eagle_rescues_Gandalf_from_Orthanc_by_Alexander_Korotich.jpg/255px-Gwaihir_the_Eagle_rescues_Gandalf_from_Orthanc_by_Alexander_Korotich.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Gwaihir_the_Eagle_rescues_Gandalf_from_Orthanc_by_Alexander_Korotich.jpg/340px-Gwaihir_the_Eagle_rescues_Gandalf_from_Orthanc_by_Alexander_Korotich.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="736" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Gwaihir" class="mw-redirect" title="Gwaihir">Gwaihir</a> the Eagle rescues Gandalf from <a href="/wiki/Orthanc" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthanc">Orthanc</a>. <a href="/wiki/Scraperboard" class="mw-redirect" title="Scraperboard">Scraperboard</a> illustration by <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Korotich" title="Alexander Korotich">Alexander Korotich</a>, 1981</figcaption></figure>
<p>Gandalf spent the years between <i>The Hobbit</i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> travelling <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a> in search of information on <a href="/wiki/Sauron" title="Sauron">Sauron</a>'s resurgence and <a href="/wiki/Bilbo_Baggins" title="Bilbo Baggins">Bilbo Baggins</a>'s mysterious <a href="/wiki/One_Ring" title="One Ring">ring</a>, spurred particularly by Bilbo's initial misleading story of how he had obtained it as a "present" from <a href="/wiki/Gollum" title="Gollum">Gollum</a>. During this period, he befriended <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a> and became suspicious of <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">Saruman</a>. He spent as much time as he could in <a href="/wiki/The_Shire" title="The Shire">the Shire</a>, strengthening his friendship with Bilbo and <a href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins" title="Frodo Baggins">Frodo</a>, Bilbo's orphaned cousin and adopted heir.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Council_of_Elrond_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Council_of_Elrond-16">&#91;T 13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gandalf returns to the Shire for Bilbo's "eleventy-first" (111th) birthday party, bringing many <a href="/wiki/Fireworks" title="Fireworks">fireworks</a> for the occasion. After Bilbo, as a prank on his guests, puts on the ring and disappears, Gandalf urges his old friend to leave the ring to Frodo, as they had planned. Bilbo becomes hostile, accusing Gandalf of trying to steal the ring. Alarmed, Gandalf tells Bilbo that is foolish. Coming to his senses, Bilbo admits that the ring has been troubling him, and leaves it behind for Frodo as he departs for <a href="/wiki/Rivendell" title="Rivendell">Rivendell</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;T 14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Over the next 17 years, Gandalf travels extensively, searching for answers on the ring. He finds some answers in Isildur's scroll, in the archives of <a href="/wiki/Minas_Tirith" title="Minas Tirith">Minas Tirith</a>. Gandalf searches long and hard for Gollum, often assisted by Aragorn, who eventually succeeds in capturing Gollum. Gandalf questions Gollum, threatening him with fire when he proves unwilling to speak. Gandalf learns that Sauron had imprisoned Gollum in his fortress of <a href="/wiki/Barad-d%C3%BBr" class="mw-redirect" title="Barad-dûr">Barad-dûr</a>, and tortured him to reveal what he knew of the <a href="/wiki/One_Ring" title="One Ring">Ring</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Council_of_Elrond_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Council_of_Elrond-16">&#91;T 13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Returning to <a href="/wiki/The_Shire" title="The Shire">the Shire</a>, Gandalf confirms his suspicion by throwing the Ring into Frodo's hearth-fire and reading the writing that appears on its surface. He tells Frodo the history of the ring, and urges him to take it to <a href="/wiki/Rivendell" title="Rivendell">Rivendell</a>, warning of grave danger if he stays in the Shire. Gandalf says he will attempt to return for Frodo's 50th birthday party, to accompany him on the road; and that meanwhile Frodo should arrange to leave quietly, as the servants of Sauron will be searching for him.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;T 15&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Outside the Shire, Gandalf encounters the wizard <a href="/wiki/Radagast_the_Brown" class="mw-redirect" title="Radagast the Brown">Radagast the Brown</a>, who brings the news that the <a href="/wiki/Nazg%C3%BBl" title="Nazgûl">Nazgûl</a> have ridden out of Mordor—and a request from <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">Saruman</a> that Gandalf come to <a href="/wiki/Isengard" title="Isengard">Isengard</a>. Gandalf asks him to send out animals to observe the Nazgûl, and to report to him at Isengard. Gandalf leaves a letter to Frodo (urging his immediate departure) with Barliman Butterbur at the <a href="/wiki/Prancing_Pony" class="mw-redirect" title="Prancing Pony">Prancing Pony</a>, and heads towards Isengard. There, Saruman horrifies Gandalf by asking him to help him to obtain and use the Ring. Gandalf refuses, and Saruman imprisons him at the top of <a href="/wiki/Orthanc" class="mw-redirect" title="Orthanc">his tower</a>. Gandalf is rescued by <a href="/wiki/Gwaihir" class="mw-redirect" title="Gwaihir">Gwaihir the Eagle</a>, who comes to him as requested via Radagast.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Council_of_Elrond_16-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Council_of_Elrond-16">&#91;T 13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="/wiki/Rohan_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rohan (Middle-earth)">Rohan</a>, Gandalf appeals to King <a href="/wiki/Th%C3%A9oden" title="Théoden">Théoden</a> for a horse. Théoden, under the evil influence of <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%ADma_Wormtongue" title="Gríma Wormtongue">Gríma Wormtongue</a>, Saruman's spy and servant, tells Gandalf to take any horse he pleases, but to leave quickly. It is then that Gandalf meets the great horse <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth#Sapient_animals" title="Middle-earth">Shadowfax</a>, who will be his mount and companion. Gandalf rides hard for the Shire, but does not reach it until after Frodo has set out. Knowing that Frodo and his companions will be heading for Rivendell, Gandalf makes his own way there. He learns at Bree that the Hobbits have fallen in with Aragorn. He faces the Nazgûl at <a href="/wiki/Weathertop" class="mw-redirect" title="Weathertop">Weathertop</a>, but escapes after an all-night battle, drawing four of them northward.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Council_of_Elrond_16-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Council_of_Elrond-16">&#91;T 13&#93;</a></sup> Frodo, Aragorn and company face the remaining five on Weathertop a few nights later.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;T 16&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf reaches Rivendell just before Frodo's arrival.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Council_of_Elrond_16-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Council_of_Elrond-16">&#91;T 13&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Rivendell, Gandalf helps <a href="/wiki/Elrond" title="Elrond">Elrond</a> drive off the Nazgûl pursuing Frodo, and plays a leading role in the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Elrond" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Elrond">Council of Elrond</a> as the only person who knows the full history of the ring. He reveals that Saruman has betrayed them and is in league with Sauron. When it is decided that the Ring has to be destroyed, Gandalf volunteers to accompany Frodo—now the Ring-bearer—in his quest. He persuades Elrond to let Frodo's cousins <a href="/wiki/Meriadoc_Brandybuck" class="mw-redirect" title="Meriadoc Brandybuck">Merry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peregrin_Took" class="mw-redirect" title="Peregrin Took">Pippin</a> join the <a href="/wiki/Fellowship_of_the_Ring_(characters)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellowship of the Ring (characters)">Fellowship</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Council_of_Elrond_16-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Council_of_Elrond-16">&#91;T 13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1210818076">.mw-parser-output .quotebox{background-color:#F9F9F9;border:1px solid #aaa;box-sizing:border-box;padding:10px;font-size:88%;max-width:100%}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft{margin:.5em 1.4em .8em 0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright{margin:.5em 0 .8em 1.4em}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.centered{overflow:hidden;position:relative;margin:.5em auto .8em auto}.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatleft span,.mw-parser-output .quotebox.floatright span{font-style:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox>blockquote{margin:0;padding:0;border-left:0;font-family:inherit;font-size:inherit}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-title{background-color:#F9F9F9;text-align:center;font-size:110%;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote>:first-child{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote:last-child>:last-child{margin-bottom:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:before{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" “ ";vertical-align:-45%;line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox-quote.quoted:after{font-family:"Times New Roman",serif;font-weight:bold;font-size:large;color:gray;content:" ” ";line-height:0}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .left-aligned{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .right-aligned{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .center-aligned{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quote-title,.mw-parser-output .quotebox .quotebox-quote{display:block}.mw-parser-output .quotebox cite{display:block;font-style:normal}@media screen and (max-width:640px){.mw-parser-output .quotebox{width:100%!important;margin:0 0 .8em!important;float:none!important}}</style><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:40%; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>The Balrog reached the bridge. Gandalf stood in the middle of the span, leaning on the staff in his left hand, but in his other hand <a href="/wiki/Glamdring" class="mw-redirect" title="Glamdring">Glamdring</a> gleamed, cold and white. His enemy halted again, facing him, and the shadow about it reached out like two vast wings. It raised the whip, and the thongs whined and cracked. Fire came from its nostrils. But Gandalf stood firm. "You cannot pass," he said. The <a href="/wiki/Orc_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orc (Middle-earth)">orcs</a> stood still, and a dead silence fell. "I am a servant of the <a href="/wiki/Secret_Fire" class="mw-redirect" title="Secret Fire">Secret Fire</a>, wielder of the flame of Anor. You cannot pass. The dark fire will not avail you, flame of <a href="/wiki/Utumno" class="mw-redirect" title="Utumno">Udûn</a>. Go back to the Shadow! You cannot pass."
</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="padding-bottom: 0em;"><cite class="left-aligned" style=""><a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a>,&#32;<i><a href="/wiki/The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Fellowship of the Ring">The Fellowship of the Ring</a></i></cite></p>
</div>
<p>Taking charge of the Fellowship (comprising nine representatives of the free peoples of <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a>, "set against the Nine Riders"), Gandalf and Aragorn lead the Hobbits and their companions south.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;T 17&#93;</a></sup> After an unsuccessful attempt to cross Mount <a href="/wiki/Caradhras" class="mw-redirect" title="Caradhras">Caradhras</a> in winter, they cross under the mountains through the Mines of <a href="/wiki/Moria_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moria (Middle-earth)">Moria</a> under the Misty Mountains, though only <a href="/wiki/Gimli_(Middle-earth)" title="Gimli (Middle-earth)">Gimli</a> the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dwarf (Middle-earth)">Dwarf</a> is enthusiastic about that route. In Moria, they discover that the dwarf colony established there by <a href="/wiki/Balin_(Middle-earth)" title="Balin (Middle-earth)">Balin</a> has been annihilated by <a href="/wiki/Orc_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Orc (Middle-earth)">orcs</a>. The Fellowship fights with the orcs and trolls of Moria and escapes them.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;T 18&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>At the <a href="/wiki/Bridge_of_Khazad-d%C3%BBm" class="mw-redirect" title="Bridge of Khazad-dûm">Bridge of Khazad-dûm</a>, they encounter "Durin's Bane," a fearsome <a href="/wiki/Balrog" title="Balrog">Balrog</a> from ancient times. Gandalf faces the Balrog to enable the others to escape. After a brief exchange of blows, Gandalf breaks the bridge beneath the Balrog with his <a href="/wiki/Magic_(Middle-earth)#Magic_items" class="mw-redirect" title="Magic (Middle-earth)">staff</a>. As the Balrog falls, it wraps its whip around Gandalf's legs, dragging him over the edge. Gandalf falls into the abyss, crying "Fly, you fools!".<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;T 19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gandalf and the Balrog fall into a deep lake in Moria's underworld. Gandalf pursues the Balrog through the tunnels for eight days until they climb to the peak of <a href="/wiki/Minor_places_in_Middle-earth#Celebdil" class="mw-redirect" title="Minor places in Middle-earth">Zirakzigil</a>. Here they fight for two days and nights. The Balrog is defeated and cast down onto the mountainside. Gandalf also dies, and his body lies on the peak while his spirit travels "out of thought and time".<sup id="cite_ref-The_White_Rider_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_White_Rider-23">&#91;T 20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><span class="anchor" id="Gandalf_the_White"></span>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Gandalf_the_White">Gandalf the White</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Gandalf the White"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Gandalf is "sent back"<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;b&#93;</a></sup> as Gandalf the White, and returns to life on the mountain top. Gwaihir carries him to <a href="/wiki/Lothl%C3%B3rien" title="Lothlórien">Lothlórien</a>, where he is healed of his injuries and re-clothed in white robes by <a href="/wiki/Galadriel" title="Galadriel">Galadriel</a>. He travels to <a href="/wiki/Fangorn" class="mw-redirect" title="Fangorn">Fangorn</a> Forest, where he encounters <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gimli_(Middle-earth)" title="Gimli (Middle-earth)">Gimli</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Legolas" title="Legolas">Legolas</a> (who are tracking <a href="/wiki/Meriadoc_Brandybuck" class="mw-redirect" title="Meriadoc Brandybuck">Merry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peregrin_Took" class="mw-redirect" title="Peregrin Took">Pippin</a>). They mistake him for <a href="/wiki/Saruman" title="Saruman">Saruman</a>, but he stops their attacks and reveals himself.<sup id="cite_ref-The_White_Rider_23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_White_Rider-23">&#91;T 20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>They travel to <a href="/wiki/Rohan_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Rohan (Middle-earth)">Rohan</a>, where Gandalf finds that Théoden has been further weakened by Wormtongue's influence. He breaks Wormtongue's hold over Théoden, and convinces the king to join in the fight against Sauron.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;T 21&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf sets off to gather warriors of the Westfold to assist Théoden in the coming battle with Saruman. Gandalf arrives just in time to defeat Saruman's army in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Helm%27s_Deep" title="Battle of Helm&#39;s Deep">battle of Helm's Deep</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;T 22&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf and the King ride to <a href="/wiki/Isengard" title="Isengard">Isengard</a>, which has just been destroyed by <a href="/wiki/Treebeard" title="Treebeard">Treebeard</a> and his <a href="/wiki/Ent" title="Ent">Ents</a>, who are accompanied by Merry and Pippin.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;T 23&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf breaks Saruman's staff and expels him from the White Council and the Order of <a href="/wiki/Wizard_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Wizard (Middle-earth)">Wizards</a>; Gandalf takes Saruman's place as head of both. Wormtongue tries to kill Gandalf or Saruman with the <i><a href="/wiki/Palant%C3%ADr" title="Palantír">palantír</a></i> of Orthanc, but misses both. Pippin retrieves the <i>palantír</i>, but Gandalf quickly takes it.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;T 24&#93;</a></sup> After the group leaves Isengard, Pippin takes the <i>palantír</i> from a sleeping Gandalf, looks into it, and comes face to face with Sauron himself. Gandalf gives the <i>palantír</i> to Aragorn and takes the chastened Pippin with him to <a href="/wiki/Minas_Tirith" title="Minas Tirith">Minas Tirith</a> to keep the young Hobbit out of further trouble.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;T 25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gandalf arrives in time to help to arrange the defences of Minas Tirith. His presence is resented by <a href="/wiki/Denethor" title="Denethor">Denethor</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Steward_of_Gondor" class="mw-redirect" title="Steward of Gondor">Steward of Gondor</a>; but when his son <a href="/wiki/Faramir" title="Faramir">Faramir</a> is gravely wounded in battle, Denethor sinks into despair and madness. Together with Prince Imrahil, Gandalf leads the defenders during the siege of the city. When the forces of <a href="/wiki/Mordor" title="Mordor">Mordor</a> break the main gate, Gandalf, alone on Shadowfax, confronts the Lord of the Nazgûl. At that moment the Rohirrim arrive, causing the Nazgûl to withdraw. Gandalf is about to pursue, but is stopped by Pippin, who requests his intervention to save Faramir – Denethor in desperation was seeking to burn himself and his son on a funeral pyre.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;T 26&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf saves Faramir (but not Denethor, who immolates himself), and plays no further part in the unfolding <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Pelennor_Fields" title="Battle of the Pelennor Fields">Battle of the Pelennor Fields</a>.
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1210818076"><div class="quotebox pullquote floatright" style="width:40%; ;">
<blockquote class="quotebox-quote left-aligned" style="">
<p>"This, then, is my counsel," [said Gandalf.] "We have not the Ring. In wisdom or great folly it has been sent away to be destroyed, lest it destroy us. Without it we cannot by force defeat [Sauron's] force. But we must at all costs keep his Eye from his true peril... We must call out his hidden strength, so that he shall empty his land... We must make ourselves the bait, though his jaws should close on us... We must walk open-eyed into that trap, with courage, but small hope for ourselves. For, my lords, it may well prove that we ourselves shall perish utterly in a black battle far from the living lands; so that even if <a href="/wiki/Barad-d%C3%BBr" class="mw-redirect" title="Barad-dûr">Barad-dûr</a> be thrown down, we shall not live to see a new age. But this, I deem, is our duty."
</p>
</blockquote>
<p style="padding-bottom: 0em;"><cite class="left-aligned" style=""><a href="/wiki/J._R._R._Tolkien" title="J. R. R. Tolkien">J. R. R. Tolkien</a>,&#32;<i><a href="/wiki/The_Return_of_the_King" title="The Return of the King">The Return of the King</a></i></cite></p>
</div>
<p>After the battle, Gandalf counsels an attack against Sauron's forces at the <a href="/wiki/Black_Gate_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Black Gate (Middle-earth)">Black Gate</a>, in an effort to distract the Dark Lord's attention from <a href="/wiki/Frodo_Baggins" title="Frodo Baggins">Frodo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sam_Gamgee" class="mw-redirect" title="Sam Gamgee">Sam</a>; they are at that moment scaling <a href="/wiki/Mount_Doom" class="mw-redirect" title="Mount Doom">Mount Doom</a> to destroy the Ring. Gandalf, Aragorn and the other leaders of the West lead an army to the Black Gate, meeting the <a href="/wiki/Mouth_of_Sauron" class="mw-redirect" title="Mouth of Sauron">nameless lieutenant of Mordor</a>, who shows them Frodo's <i><a href="/wiki/Mithril" title="Mithril">mithril</a></i> shirt and other items from the Hobbits' equipment. Gandalf rejects Mordor's terms of surrender, starting the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Morannon" title="Battle of the Morannon">Battle of the Morannon</a>. The forces of the West face the full might of Sauron's armies, until the Ring is destroyed in Mount Doom.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;T 27&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf leads the Eagles to rescue Frodo and Sam from the erupting mountain.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;T 28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the war, Gandalf crowns Aragorn as King Elessar, and helps him find a sapling of the <a href="/wiki/White_Tree_of_Gondor" class="mw-redirect" title="White Tree of Gondor">White Tree of Gondor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;T 29&#93;</a></sup> He accompanies the Hobbits back to the borders of <a href="/wiki/The_Shire" title="The Shire">the Shire</a>, before leaving to visit <a href="/wiki/Tom_Bombadil" title="Tom Bombadil">Tom Bombadil</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;T 30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Two years later, Gandalf departs <a href="/wiki/Middle-earth" title="Middle-earth">Middle-earth</a> forever. He boards the Ringbearers' ship in the Grey Havens and sets sail to return across <a href="/wiki/Belegaer" class="mw-redirect" title="Belegaer">the sea</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Undying_Lands" class="mw-redirect" title="Undying Lands">Undying Lands</a>; with him are his horse Shadowfax and his friends Frodo, <a href="/wiki/Bilbo_Baggins" title="Bilbo Baggins">Bilbo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galadriel" title="Galadriel">Galadriel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Elrond" title="Elrond">Elrond</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;T 31&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Concept_and_creation">Concept and creation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Concept and creation"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Appearance">Appearance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Appearance"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1096954695/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .multiimageinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:370px;max-width:370px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:172px;max-width:172px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:235px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Der_Berggeist.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/33/Der_Berggeist.jpg/170px-Der_Berggeist.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="236" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/33/Der_Berggeist.jpg/255px-Der_Berggeist.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/3/33/Der_Berggeist.jpg 2x" data-file-width="268" data-file-height="372" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption"><i>Der Berggeist</i> by <a href="/wiki/Josef_Madlener" title="Josef Madlener">Josef Madlener</a></div></div><div class="tsingle" style="width:194px;max-width:194px"><div class="thumbimage" style="border:none;;height:235px;overflow:hidden"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:V%C3%A4in%C3%A4m%C3%B6inen_in_Sammon_puolustus.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/V%C3%A4in%C3%A4m%C3%B6inen_in_Sammon_puolustus.jpg/192px-V%C3%A4in%C3%A4m%C3%B6inen_in_Sammon_puolustus.jpg" decoding="async" width="192" height="235" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/V%C3%A4in%C3%A4m%C3%B6inen_in_Sammon_puolustus.jpg/288px-V%C3%A4in%C3%A4m%C3%B6inen_in_Sammon_puolustus.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/V%C3%A4in%C3%A4m%C3%B6inen_in_Sammon_puolustus.jpg/384px-V%C3%A4in%C3%A4m%C3%B6inen_in_Sammon_puolustus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="891" data-file-height="1092" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Väinämöinen as depicted by <a href="/wiki/Akseli_Gallen-Kallela" title="Akseli Gallen-Kallela">Akseli Gallen-Kallela</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Defense_of_the_Sampo" title="The Defense of the Sampo">The Defense of the Sampo</a></i> (1896)</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Tolkien's biographer <a href="/wiki/Humphrey_Carpenter" title="Humphrey Carpenter">Humphrey Carpenter</a> relates that Tolkien owned a postcard entitled <i>Der Berggeist</i> ("the mountain spirit"), which he labelled "the origin of Gandalf".<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> It shows a white-bearded man in a large hat and cloak seated among boulders in a mountain forest. Carpenter said that Tolkien recalled buying the postcard during his holiday in <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> in 1911. Manfred Zimmerman, however, discovered that the painting was by the <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">German</a> artist <a href="/wiki/Josef_Madlener" title="Josef Madlener">Josef Madlener</a> and dates from the mid-1920s. Carpenter acknowledged that Tolkien was probably mistaken about the origin of the postcard.<sup id="cite_ref-zimmerman_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-zimmerman-37">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Finnish_influences_on_Tolkien" title="Finnish influences on Tolkien">An additional influence</a> may have been <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A4in%C3%A4m%C3%B6inen" title="Väinämöinen">Väinämöinen</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Demigod" title="Demigod">demigod</a> and the central character in <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finnish</a> <a href="/wiki/Folklore" title="Folklore">folklore</a> and the <a href="/wiki/National_epic" title="National epic">national epic</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Kalevala" title="Kalevala">Kalevala</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Elias_L%C3%B6nnrot" title="Elias Lönnrot">Elias Lönnrot</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Väinämöinen was described as an old and wise man, and he possessed a potent, magical singing voice.<sup id="cite_ref-kansallisbiografia_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kansallisbiografia-39">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Throughout the early drafts, and through to the first edition of <i>The Hobbit</i>, Bladorthin/Gandalf is described as being a "little old man", distinct from a dwarf, but not of the full human stature that would later be described in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>. Even in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>, Gandalf was not tall; shorter, for example, than <a href="/wiki/Elrond" title="Elrond">Elrond</a><sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;T 32&#93;</a></sup> or the other wizards.<sup id="cite_ref-Istari_2-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Istari-2">&#91;T 1&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Name"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>When writing <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit" title="The Hobbit">The Hobbit</a></i> in the early 1930s Tolkien gave the name <i>Gandalf</i> to the leader of the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dwarf (Middle-earth)">Dwarves</a>, the character later called <a href="/wiki/Thorin_Oakenshield" title="Thorin Oakenshield">Thorin Oakenshield</a>. The name is taken from the same source as all the other Dwarf names (save <a href="/wiki/Balin_(Middle-earth)" title="Balin (Middle-earth)">Balin</a>) in <i>The Hobbit</i>: the "<a href="/wiki/Norse_dwarves#Dvergatal:_the_list_of_the_Dvergar" class="mw-redirect" title="Norse dwarves">Catalogue of Dwarves</a>" in the <i><a href="/wiki/V%C3%B6lusp%C3%A1" title="Völuspá">Völuspá</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> name <i><span title="Old Norse-language text"><i lang="non">Gandalfr</i></span></i> incorporates the words <i><span title="Old Norse-language text"><i lang="non">gandr</i></span></i> meaning "wand", "staff" or (especially in compounds) "<a href="/wiki/Magic_(paranormal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Magic (paranormal)">magic</a>" and <i><span title="Old Norse-language text"><i lang="non">álfr</i></span></i> "<a href="/wiki/Elf" title="Elf">elf</a>". The name <i><a href="/wiki/Gandalf_(Norse_mythology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Gandalf (Norse mythology)">Gandalf</a></i> is found in at least one more place in Norse myth, in the semi-historical <a href="/wiki/Heimskringla" title="Heimskringla">Heimskringla</a>, which briefly describes <a href="/wiki/Gandalf_Alfgeirsson" title="Gandalf Alfgeirsson">Gandalf Alfgeirsson</a>, a legendary Norse king from eastern Norway and rival of <a href="/wiki/Halfdan_the_Black" title="Halfdan the Black">Halfdan the Black</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf is also the name of a Norse sea-king in <a href="/wiki/Henrik_Ibsen" title="Henrik Ibsen">Henrik Ibsen</a>'s second play, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Burial_Mound" title="The Burial Mound">The Burial Mound</a></i>. The name "Gandolf" occurs as a character in <a href="/wiki/William_Morris" title="William Morris">William Morris</a>' 1896 fantasy novel <i><a href="/wiki/The_Well_at_the_World%27s_End" title="The Well at the World&#39;s End">The Well at the World's End</a></i>, along with the horse "Silverfax", adapted by Tolkien as Gandalf's horse "Shadowfax". Morris' book, inspired by Norse myth, is set in a pseudo-<a href="/wiki/Medieval" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval">medieval</a> landscape; it deeply influenced Tolkien. The wizard that became Gandalf was originally named <i>Bladorthin</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;T 33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Tolkien came to regret his <i>ad hoc</i> use of <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> names, referring to a "rabble of <a href="/wiki/Elder_Edda" class="mw-redirect" title="Elder Edda">eddaic</a>-named dwarves,&#160;... invented in an idle hour" in 1937.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;T 34&#93;</a></sup> But the decision to use Old Norse names came to have far-reaching consequences in the composition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>; in 1942, Tolkien decided that the work was to be a purported translation from the <a href="/wiki/Fictional_language" title="Fictional language">fictional language</a> of <a href="/wiki/Westron" class="mw-redirect" title="Westron">Westron</a>, and in the English translation <a href="/wiki/Old_Norse" title="Old Norse">Old Norse</a> names were taken to represent names in the language of <a href="/wiki/Dale_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dale (Middle-earth)">Dale</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> <i>Gandalf</i>, in this setting, is thus a representation in English (anglicised from Old Norse) of the name the Dwarves of Erebor had given to Olórin in the language they used "externally" in their daily affairs, while <i>Tharkûn</i> is the (untranslated) name, presumably of the same meaning, that the Dwarves gave him in their native <a href="/wiki/Khuzdul" title="Khuzdul">Khuzdul</a> language.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;T 35&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Guide">Guide</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Guide"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Gandalf's role and importance was substantially increased in the conception of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings" title="The Lord of the Rings">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>, and in a letter of 1954, Tolkien refers to Gandalf as an "<a href="/wiki/Angel" title="Angel">angel</a> incarnate".<sup id="cite_ref-letters_156_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-letters_156-47">&#91;T 36&#93;</a></sup> In the same letter Tolkien states he was given the form of an old man in order to limit his powers on Earth. Both in 1965 and 1971 Tolkien again refers to Gandalf as an angelic being.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;T 37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;T 38&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In a 1946 letter, Tolkien stated that he thought of Gandalf as an "Odinic wanderer".<sup id="cite_ref-letters_107_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-letters_107-50">&#91;T 39&#93;</a></sup> Other commentators have similarly compared Gandalf to the <a href="/wiki/Norse_mythology" title="Norse mythology">Norse god</a> <a href="/wiki/Odin" title="Odin">Odin</a> in his "Wanderer" guise—an old man with one eye, a long white beard, a wide brimmed hat, and a staff,<sup id="cite_ref-Jøn_1997_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Jøn_1997-51">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Burns_2005_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Burns_2005-52">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> or likened him to <a href="/wiki/Merlin" title="Merlin">Merlin</a> of <a href="/wiki/Matter_of_Britain#Arthurian_cycle" title="Matter of Britain">Arthurian legend</a> or the <a href="/wiki/Jungian_archetypes" title="Jungian archetypes">Jungian archetype</a> of the "<a href="/wiki/Wise_old_man" title="Wise old man">wise old man</a>".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right: auto; border: none;">

<p>In <i><a href="/wiki/The_Annotated_Hobbit" title="The Annotated Hobbit">The Annotated Hobbit</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Douglas_A._Anderson" title="Douglas A. Anderson">Douglas Anderson</a> likens Gandalf's role to the <i><a href="/wiki/R%C3%BCbezahl" title="Rübezahl">Rübezahl</a></i> mountain spirit of German folktales. He states that the figure can appear as "a guide, a messenger, or a farmer", often depicted as "a bearded man with a staff".<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTETolkien1937148–149_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTETolkien1937148–149-55">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 152px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Georg_von_Rosen_-_Oden_som_vandringsman,_1886_(Odin,_the_Wanderer).jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Odin, the Wanderer by Georg von Rosen, 1886[10]"><img alt="Odin, the Wanderer by Georg von Rosen, 1886[10]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Georg_von_Rosen_-_Oden_som_vandringsman%2C_1886_%28Odin%2C_the_Wanderer%29.jpg/225px-Georg_von_Rosen_-_Oden_som_vandringsman%2C_1886_%28Odin%2C_the_Wanderer%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Georg_von_Rosen_-_Oden_som_vandringsman%2C_1886_%28Odin%2C_the_Wanderer%29.jpg/337px-Georg_von_Rosen_-_Oden_som_vandringsman%2C_1886_%28Odin%2C_the_Wanderer%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/Georg_von_Rosen_-_Oden_som_vandringsman%2C_1886_%28Odin%2C_the_Wanderer%29.jpg/450px-Georg_von_Rosen_-_Oden_som_vandringsman%2C_1886_%28Odin%2C_the_Wanderer%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="733" /></a></span></div>

		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 158.66666666667px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 156.66666666667px;"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:GANDALF.jpg" class="mw-file-description" title="Gandalf, by &#39;Nidoart&#39;, 2013"><img alt="Gandalf, by &#39;Nidoart&#39;, 2013" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/GANDALF.jpg/235px-GANDALF.jpg" decoding="async" width="157" height="220" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/GANDALF.jpg/353px-GANDALF.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ea/GANDALF.jpg/471px-GANDALF.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1071" data-file-height="1500" /></a></span></div>
