</ul>
<p>The Tolkien scholar Charles W. Nelson described Gandalf as a "guide who .. assists a major character on a journey or quest .. to unusual and distant places". He noted that in both <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> and <i>The Hobbit</i>, Tolkien presents Gandalf in these terms. Immediately after the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Elrond" class="mw-redirect" title="Council of Elrond">Council of Elrond</a>, Gandalf tells the <a href="/wiki/Fellowship_of_the_Ring_(characters)" class="mw-redirect" title="Fellowship of the Ring (characters)">Fellowship</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_2002_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2002-56">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1211633275"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>Someone said that intelligence would be needed in the party. He was right. I think I shall come with you.<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_2002_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2002-56">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>Nelson notes the similarity between this and <a href="/wiki/Thorin_Oakenshield" title="Thorin Oakenshield">Thorin</a>'s statement in <i>The Hobbit</i>:<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_2002_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2002-56">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1211633275"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We shall soon .. start on our long journey, a journey from which some of us, or perhaps all of us (except our friend and counsellor, the ingenious wizard Gandalf) may never return.<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_2002_56-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2002-56">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Dante_and_Virgil_on_the_ice_of_lake_Leucocytes.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Dante_and_Virgil_on_the_ice_of_lake_Leucocytes.jpg/220px-Dante_and_Virgil_on_the_ice_of_lake_Leucocytes.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Dante_and_Virgil_on_the_ice_of_lake_Leucocytes.jpg/330px-Dante_and_Virgil_on_the_ice_of_lake_Leucocytes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Dante_and_Virgil_on_the_ice_of_lake_Leucocytes.jpg/440px-Dante_and_Virgil_on_the_ice_of_lake_Leucocytes.jpg 2x" data-file-width="780" data-file-height="535" /></a><figcaption>Earlier guide figure: <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a> guides <a href="/wiki/Dante" class="mw-redirect" title="Dante">Dante</a> around the lowest circle of hell in <a href="/wiki/Dante" class="mw-redirect" title="Dante">Dante</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Inferno_(Dante)" title="Inferno (Dante)">Inferno</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_2002_56-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2002-56">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Painting by <a href="/wiki/Gustave_Dor%C3%A9" title="Gustave Doré">Gustave Doré</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>Nelson gives as examples of the guide figure the <a href="/wiki/Cumaean_Sibyl" title="Cumaean Sibyl">Cumaean Sibyl</a> who assisted <a href="/wiki/Aeneas" title="Aeneas">Aeneas</a> on his journey through the underworld in <a href="/wiki/Virgil" title="Virgil">Virgil</a>'s tale <i><a href="/wiki/The_Aeneid" class="mw-redirect" title="The Aeneid">The Aeneid</a></i>, and then Virgil himself in <a href="/wiki/Dante" class="mw-redirect" title="Dante">Dante</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Inferno_(Dante)" title="Inferno (Dante)">Inferno</a></i>, directing, encouraging, and physically assisting Dante as he travels through hell. In English literature, Nelson notes, <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Malory" title="Thomas Malory">Thomas Malory</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Morte_d%27Arthur" title="Le Morte d&#39;Arthur">Le Morte d'Arthur</a></i> has the wizard Merlin teaching and directing <a href="/wiki/King_Arthur" title="King Arthur">Arthur</a> to begin his journeys. Given these precedents, Nelson remarks, it was unsurprising that Tolkien should make use of a guide figure, endowing him, like these predecessors, with power, wisdom, experience, and practical knowledge, and "aware[ness] of [his] own limitations and [his] ranking in the order of the great".<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_2002_56-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2002-56">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Other characters who act as wise and good guides include <a href="/wiki/Tom_Bombadil" title="Tom Bombadil">Tom Bombadil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elrond" title="Elrond">Elrond</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aragorn" title="Aragorn">Aragorn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Galadriel" title="Galadriel">Galadriel</a>—who he calls perhaps the most powerful of the guide figures—and briefly also <a href="/wiki/Faramir" title="Faramir">Faramir</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_2002_56-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2002-56">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Nelson writes that there is equally historical precedent for wicked guides, such as <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Spenser" title="Edmund Spenser">Edmund Spenser</a>'s "evil palmers" in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Faerie_Queene" title="The Faerie Queene">The Faerie Queene</a></i>, and suggests that <a href="/wiki/Gollum" title="Gollum">Gollum</a> functions as an evil guide, contrasted with Gandalf, in <i>Lord of the Rings</i>. He notes that both Gollum and Gandalf are servants of The One, <a href="/wiki/Eru_Il%C3%BAvatar" class="mw-redirect" title="Eru Ilúvatar">Eru Ilúvatar</a>, in the struggle against the forces of darkness, and "ironically" all of them, good and bad, are necessary to the success of the quest. He comments, too, that despite Gandalf's evident power, and the moment when he faces the <a href="/wiki/Nazg%C3%BBl" title="Nazgûl">Lord of the Nazgûl</a>, he stays in the role of guide throughout, "never directly confront[ing] his enemies with his raw power."<sup id="cite_ref-Nelson_2002_56-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nelson_2002-56">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christ-figure">Christ-figure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Christ-figure"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Christianity_in_Middle-earth" title="Christianity in Middle-earth">Christianity in Middle-earth</a></div>
<p>The critic Anne C. Petty, writing about "<a href="/wiki/Allegory" title="Allegory">Allegory</a>" in the <i><a href="/wiki/J.R.R._Tolkien_Encyclopedia" class="mw-redirect" title="J.R.R. Tolkien Encyclopedia">J.R.R. Tolkien Encyclopedia</a></i>, discusses Gandalf's death and reappearance in <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> terms. She cites Michael W. Maher, <a href="/wiki/Society_of_Jesus" class="mw-redirect" title="Society of Jesus">S.J.</a>: "who could not think of Gandalf's descent into the pits of Moria and his return clothed in white as a death-<a href="/wiki/Resurrection" title="Resurrection">resurrection</a> motif?"<sup id="cite_ref-Petty_2013_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petty_2013-57">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> She at once notes, however, that "such a narrow [allegorical] interpretation" limits the reader's imagination by demanding a single meaning for each character and event.<sup id="cite_ref-Petty_2013_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Petty_2013-57">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Other scholars and theologians have likened Gandalf's return as a "gleaming white" figure to the <a href="/wiki/Transfiguration_of_Jesus" title="Transfiguration of Jesus">transfiguration of Christ</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Stucky_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stucky-61">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The philosopher <a href="/wiki/Peter_Kreeft" title="Peter Kreeft">Peter Kreeft</a>, like Tolkien a <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a>, observes that there is no one complete, concrete, visible <a href="/wiki/Christ" class="mw-redirect" title="Christ">Christ</a> figure in <i>The Lord of the Rings</i> comparable to <a href="/wiki/Aslan" title="Aslan">Aslan</a> in <a href="/wiki/C._S._Lewis" title="C. S. Lewis">C. S. Lewis</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Chronicles_of_Narnia" class="mw-redirect" title="Chronicles of Narnia">Chronicles of Narnia</a> series. However, Kreeft and Jean Chausse have identified reflections of the figure of Jesus Christ in three <a href="/wiki/Protagonist" title="Protagonist">protagonists</a> of <i>The Lord of the Rings</i>: Gandalf, Frodo and Aragorn. While Chausse found "facets of the personality of Jesus" in them, Kreeft wrote that "they exemplify the Old Testament <a href="/wiki/Threefold_office" title="Threefold office">threefold Messianic symbolism</a> of <a href="/wiki/Prophet" title="Prophet">prophet</a> (Gandalf), <a href="/wiki/Priest" title="Priest">priest</a> (Frodo), and <a href="/wiki/King" title="King">king</a> (Aragorn)."<sup id="cite_ref-Kreeft_2005_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kreeft_2005-62">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<table class="wikitable" style="margin: auto">

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Adaptations">Adaptations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Adaptations"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:BakshiGandalf.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/BakshiGandalf.JPG/220px-BakshiGandalf.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/c/c3/BakshiGandalf.JPG 1.5x" data-file-width="299" data-file-height="168" /></a><figcaption>Gandalf as depicted in <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bakshi" title="Ralph Bakshi">Ralph Bakshi</a>'s <a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1978_film)" title="The Lord of the Rings (1978 film)">1978 animated film</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio" title="BBC Radio">BBC Radio</a> dramatisations, Gandalf has been voiced by <a href="/wiki/Norman_Shelley" title="Norman Shelley">Norman Shelley</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1955_radio_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (1955 radio series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> (1955–1956),<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Heron_Carvic" title="Heron Carvic">Heron Carvic</a> in <i>The Hobbit</i> (1968), <a href="/wiki/Bernard_Mayes" title="Bernard Mayes">Bernard Mayes</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1979_radio_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (1979 radio series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> (1979),<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> and Sir <a href="/wiki/Michael_Hordern" title="Michael Hordern">Michael Hordern</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1981_radio_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (1981 radio series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> (1981).<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_Huston" title="John Huston">John Huston</a> voiced Gandalf in the animated films <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(1977_film)" title="The Hobbit (1977 film)">The Hobbit</a></i> (1977) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Return_of_the_King_(1980_film)" title="The Return of the King (1980 film)">The Return of the King</a></i> (1980) produced by <a href="/wiki/Rankin/Bass" class="mw-redirect" title="Rankin/Bass">Rankin/Bass</a>. <a href="/wiki/William_Squire" title="William Squire">William Squire</a> voiced Gandalf in the animated film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(1978_film)" title="The Lord of the Rings (1978 film)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> (1978) directed by <a href="/wiki/Ralph_Bakshi" title="Ralph Bakshi">Ralph Bakshi</a>. <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Krasko_(actor)" title="Ivan Krasko (actor)">Ivan Krasko</a> played Gandalf in the Soviet film adaptation <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(1985_film)" title="The Hobbit (1985 film)">The Hobbit</a></i> (1985).<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf was portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Vesa_Vierikko" title="Vesa Vierikko">Vesa Vierikko</a> in the Finnish television <a href="/wiki/Miniseries" title="Miniseries">miniseries</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Hobitit" title="Hobitit">Hobitit</a></i> (1993).<sup id="cite_ref-Kajava_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kajava-72">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Gandalf600ppx.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Gandalf600ppx.jpg/170px-Gandalf600ppx.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="185" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Gandalf600ppx.jpg/255px-Gandalf600ppx.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e9/Gandalf600ppx.jpg 2x" data-file-width="303" data-file-height="329" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a> as Gandalf the White in <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers">The Two Towers</a></i> (2002)</figcaption></figure>
<p><a href="/wiki/Ian_McKellen" title="Ian McKellen">Ian McKellen</a> portrayed Gandalf in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings_(film_series)" title="The Lord of the Rings (film series)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i> film series (2001–2003), directed by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Jackson" title="Peter Jackson">Peter Jackson</a>, after <a href="/wiki/Sean_Connery" title="Sean Connery">Sean Connery</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Stewart" title="Patrick Stewart">Patrick Stewart</a> both turned down the role.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> According to Jackson, McKellen based his performance as Gandalf on Tolkien himself:
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1211633275"><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>We listened to audio recordings of Tolkien reading excerpts from <i>Lord of the Rings</i>. We watched some BBC interviews with him—there's a few interviews with Tolkien—and Ian based his performance on an impersonation of Tolkien. He's literally basing Gandalf on Tolkien. He sounds the same, he uses the speech patterns and his mannerisms are born out of the same roughness from the footage of Tolkien. So, Tolkien would recognize himself in Ian's performance.<sup id="cite_ref-impersonate_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-impersonate-75">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup></p></blockquote>
<p>McKellen received widespread acclaim<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> for his portrayal of Gandalf, particularly in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Fellowship_of_the_Ring" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Fellowship of the Ring">The Fellowship of the Ring</a></i>, for which he received a <a href="/wiki/Screen_Actors_Guild_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Screen Actors Guild Award">Screen Actors Guild Award</a><sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> and an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor">Academy Award nomination, both for best supporting actor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" class="mw-redirect" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> named Gandalf, as portrayed by McKellen, the 30th greatest film character of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He reprised the role in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hobbit_(film_series)" title="The Hobbit (film series)">The Hobbit</a></i> film series (2012–2014), claiming that he enjoyed playing Gandalf the Grey more than Gandalf the White.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> He voiced Gandalf for several video games based on the films, including <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Two_Towers_(video_game)" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Two Towers (video game)">The Two Towers</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Return_of_the_King_(video_game)" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Return of the King (video game)">The Return of the King</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lord_of_the_Rings:_The_Third_Age" title="The Lord of the Rings: The Third Age">The Third Age</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>Charles Picard portrayed Gandalf in the 1999 stage production of <i>The Two Towers</i> at <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">Chicago</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Lifeline_Theatre" title="Lifeline Theatre">Lifeline Theatre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Brent_Carver" title="Brent Carver">Brent Carver</a> portrayed Gandalf in the 2006 musical production <i><a href="/wiki/Lord_of_the_Rings_(musical)" title="Lord of the Rings (musical)">The Lord of the Rings</a></i>, which opened in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gandalf appears in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Lego_Movie" title="The Lego Movie">The Lego Movie</a></i>, voiced by <a href="/wiki/Todd_Hanson" title="Todd Hanson">Todd Hanson</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Gandalf is a main character in the video game <i><a href="/wiki/Lego_Dimensions" title="Lego Dimensions">Lego Dimensions</a></i> and is voiced by <a href="/wiki/Tom_Kane" title="Tom Kane">Tom Kane</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Gandalf has his own movement in <a href="/wiki/Johan_de_Meij" title="Johan de Meij">Johan de Meij's</a> <a href="/wiki/Symphony_No._1_%22The_Lord_of_the_Rings%22" class="mw-redirect" title="Symphony No. 1 &quot;The Lord of the Rings&quot;">Symphony No. 1 "The Lord of the Rings"</a>, which was written for <a href="/wiki/Concert_band" title="Concert band">concert band</a> and premiered in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The Gandalf theme has the note sequence G-A-D-A-F, "Gandalf" as far as can be formed with the notes A to G. The result is a "striving, rising theme".<sup id="cite_ref-Bratman_2010_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bratman_2010-91">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Gandalf&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notes"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1011085734">.mw-parser-output .reflist{font-size:90%;margin-bottom:0.5em;list-style-type:decimal}.mw-parser-output .reflist .references{font-size:100%;margin-bottom:0;list-style-type:inherit}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-2{column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns-3{column-width:25em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns{margin-top:0.3em}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns ol{margin-top:0}.mw-parser-output .reflist-columns li{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-alpha{list-style-type:upper-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-upper-roman{list-style-type:upper-roman}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-alpha{list-style-type:lower-alpha}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-greek{list-style-type:lower-greek}.mw-parser-output .reflist-lower-roman{list-style-type:lower-roman}</style><div class="reflist reflist-lower-alpha">
<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">
<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Meaning "Grey Pilgrim"</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-24">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In <i>Letters</i>, #156, Tolkien clearly implies that the "Authority" that sent Gandalf back was above the <a href="/wiki/Vala_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vala (Middle-earth)">Valar</a> (who are bound by <a href="/wiki/Arda_(Middle-earth)" class="mw-redirect" title="Arda (Middle-earth)">Arda</a>'s space and time, while Gandalf went beyond time). He clearly intends this as an example of <a href="/wiki/Eru_Il%C3%BAvatar" class="mw-redirect" title="Eru Ilúvatar">Eru</a> intervening to change the course of the world.</span>
</li>
<li id="cite_note-66"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-66">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Other commentators such as <a href="/wiki/Jane_Chance" title="Jane Chance">Jane Chance</a> have compared this transformed reappearance to the <a href="/wiki/Transfiguration_of_Jesus" title="Transfiguration of Jesus">Transfiguration of Jesus</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></span>
</li>
</ol></div></div>
